<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Algae</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Group of eukaryotic organisms</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Alga" redirects here. For places called Alga, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Alga_(disambiguation)" title="Alga (disambiguation)">Alga (disambiguation)</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Algae_(disambiguation)" title="Algae (disambiguation)">Algae (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Algae</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">dʒ</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>, <wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; singular <b>alga</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is an informal term for a large, diverse group of <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthetic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eukaryotic" title="Eukaryotic">eukaryotic</a> <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a> that are not necessarily closely related, and is thus <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polyphyletic" title="Polyphyletic">polyphyletic</a>. Included organisms range from <a href="/wiki/Unicellular_organism" title="Unicellular organism">unicellular</a> <a href="/wiki/Microalgae" title="Microalgae">microalgae</a> genera, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Chlorella" title="Chlorella">Chlorella</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Diatom" title="Diatom">diatoms</a>, to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multicellular" title="Multicellular">multicellular</a> forms, such as  the <a href="/wiki/Macrocystis_pyrifera" title="Macrocystis pyrifera">giant kelp</a>, a large <a href="/wiki/Brown_algae" title="Brown algae">brown alga</a> which may grow up to 50 m in length. Most are aquatic and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autotrophic" title="Autotrophic">autotrophic</a> and lack many of the distinct cell and tissue types, such as <a href="/wiki/Stoma" title="Stoma">stomata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xylem" title="Xylem">xylem</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Phloem" title="Phloem">phloem</a>, which are found in <a href="/wiki/Embryophyte" title="Embryophyte">land plants</a>. The largest and most complex marine algae are called <a href="/wiki/Seaweed" title="Seaweed">seaweeds</a>, while the most complex freshwater forms are the <a href="/wiki/Charophyta" title="Charophyta">Charophyta</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">division</a> of green algae which includes, for example, <i><a href="/wiki/Spirogyra" title="Spirogyra">Spirogyra</a></i> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stonewort" title="Stonewort">stoneworts</a>.
</p><p>No definition of algae is generally accepted. One definition is that algae "have <a href="/wiki/Chlorophyll" title="Chlorophyll">chlorophyll</a> as their primary photosynthetic pigment and lack a sterile covering of cells around their reproductive cells".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Cyanobacteria" title="Cyanobacteria">cyanobacteria</a> are often referred to as "blue-green algae", most authorities exclude all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prokaryotes" title="Prokaryotes">prokaryotes</a> from the definition of algae.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IntroBot_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-IntroBot-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allaby_92_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allaby_92-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algae constitute a polyphyletic group<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IntroBot_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-IntroBot-3">[3]</a></sup> since they do not include a common ancestor, and although their <a href="/wiki/Plastid" title="Plastid">plastids</a> seem to have a single origin, from cyanobacteria,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keeling_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-keeling-5">[5]</a></sup> they were acquired in different ways. <a href="/wiki/Green_algae" title="Green algae">Green algae</a> are examples of algae that have primary <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">chloroplasts</a> derived from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endosymbiotic_theory" title="Endosymbiotic theory">endosymbiotic</a> cyanobacteria. <a href="/wiki/Diatom" title="Diatom">Diatoms</a> and brown algae are examples of algae with secondary chloroplasts derived from an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endosymbiotic_theory#Secondary_endosymbiosis" title="Endosymbiotic theory">endosymbiotic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_alga" title="Red alga">red alga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algae exhibit a wide range of reproductive strategies, from simple <a href="/wiki/Asexual_reproduction" title="Asexual reproduction">asexual</a> cell division to complex forms of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_reproduction" title="Sexual reproduction">sexual reproduction</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Algae lack the various structures that characterize land plants, such as the phyllids (leaf-like structures) of <a href="/wiki/Bryophyte" title="Bryophyte">bryophytes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhizoid" title="Rhizoid">rhizoids</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nonvascular_plants" title="Nonvascular plants">nonvascular plants</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Root" title="Root">roots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leaf" title="Leaf">leaves</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" title="Organ (anatomy)">organs</a> found in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tracheophyte" title="Tracheophyte">tracheophytes</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vascular_plants" title="Vascular plants">vascular plants</a>). Most are <a href="/wiki/Phototroph" title="Phototroph">phototrophic</a>, although some are <a href="/wiki/Mixotroph" title="Mixotroph">mixotrophic</a>, deriving energy both from photosynthesis and uptake of organic carbon either by <a href="/wiki/Osmotrophy" title="Osmotrophy">osmotrophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myzocytosis" title="Myzocytosis">myzotrophy</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Phagocytosis" title="Phagocytosis">phagotrophy</a>. Some unicellular species of <a href="/wiki/Green_algae" title="Green algae">green algae</a>, many <a href="/wiki/Golden_algae" title="Golden algae">golden algae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euglenid" title="Euglenid">euglenids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinoflagellate" title="Dinoflagellate">dinoflagellates</a>, and other algae have become <a href="/wiki/Heterotroph" title="Heterotroph">heterotrophs</a> (also called colorless or apochlorotic algae), sometimes parasitic, relying entirely on external energy sources and have limited or no photosynthetic apparatus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Some other heterotrophic organisms, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apicomplexans" title="Apicomplexans">apicomplexans</a>, are also derived from cells whose ancestors possessed plastids, but are not traditionally considered as algae. Algae have photosynthetic machinery ultimately derived from <a href="/wiki/Cyanobacteria" title="Cyanobacteria">cyanobacteria</a> that produce <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> as a by-product of photosynthesis, unlike other photosynthetic bacteria such as <a href="/wiki/Purple_sulfur_bacteria" title="Purple sulfur bacteria">purple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green_sulfur_bacteria" title="Green sulfur bacteria">green sulfur bacteria</a>. Fossilized filamentous algae from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vindhya" title="Vindhya">Vindhya</a> basin have been dated back to 1.6 to 1.7 billion years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_study">Etymology and study</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and study">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The singular <i>alga</i> is the Latin word for "seaweed" and retains that meaning in English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Etymology" title="Etymology">etymology</a> is obscure. Although some speculate that it is related to Latin <i>algēre</i>, "be cold",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> no reason is known to associate seaweed with temperature. A more likely source is <i>alliga</i>, "binding, entwining".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> word for seaweed was φῦκος (<i>phŷcos</i>), which could mean either the seaweed (probably red algae) or a red dye derived from it. The Latinization, <i>fūcus</i>, meant primarily the cosmetic rouge. The etymology is uncertain, but a strong candidate has long been some word related to the Biblical פוך (<i>pūk</i>), "paint" (if not that word itself), a cosmetic eye-shadow used by the ancient Egyptians and other inhabitants of the eastern Mediterranean. It could be any color: black, red, green, or blue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Accordingly, the modern study of marine and freshwater algae is called either <a href="/wiki/Phycology" title="Phycology">phycology</a> or algology, depending on whether the Greek or Latin root is used. The name <i>Fucus</i> appears in a number of <a href="/wiki/Taxon" title="Taxon">taxa</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Classification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="extiw" href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Algae" title="wikispecies:Algae">wikispecies:Algae</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gephyrocapsa_oceanica_color.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gephyrocapsa_oceanica_color.jpg/220px-Gephyrocapsa_oceanica_color.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gephyrocapsa_oceanica_color.jpg/330px-Gephyrocapsa_oceanica_color.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Gephyrocapsa_oceanica_color.jpg/440px-Gephyrocapsa_oceanica_color.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gephyrocapsa_oceanica_color.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>False-color <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scanning_electron_micrograph" title="Scanning electron micrograph">scanning electron micrograph</a> of the unicellular <a href="/wiki/Coccolithophore" title="Coccolithophore">coccolithophore</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Gephyrocapsa" title="Gephyrocapsa">Gephyrocapsa</a> oceanica</i></div></div></div>
<p>The algae contain <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">chloroplasts</a> that are similar in structure to cyanobacteria. Chloroplasts contain circular <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> like that in cyanobacteria and are interpreted as representing reduced endosymbiotic cyanobacteria. However, the exact origin of the chloroplasts is different among separate lineages of algae, reflecting their acquisition during different endosymbiotic events. The table below describes the composition of the three major groups of algae. Their lineage relationships are shown in the figure in the upper right. Many of these groups contain some members that are no longer photosynthetic. Some retain plastids, but not chloroplasts, while others have lost plastids entirely.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phylogeny" title="Phylogeny">Phylogeny</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Plastid" title="Plastid">plastid</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bhattacharya1998_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bhattacharya1998-16">[16]</a></sup> not nucleocytoplasmic genealogy:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r853264556">.mw-parser-output table.clade{border-spacing:0;margin:0;font-size:100%;line-height:100%;border-collapse:separate;width:auto}.mw-parser-output table.clade table.clade{width:100%}.mw-parser-output table.clade td{border:0;padding:0;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label{width:0.8em;border:0;padding:0 0.2em;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel{border:0;padding:0 0.2em;vertical-align:top;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-bar{vertical-align:middle;text-align:left;padding:0 0.5em}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leaf{border:0;padding:0;text-align:left;vertical-align:middle}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leafR{border:0;padding:0;text-align:right}</style>
